+ First-person unique perspective: Overthinking It — Score: 82.0
Prompt:
Overthinking It Write a first-person narrative from the perspective of an intelligent 8th-grade girl with social anxiety who has developed a crush on a classmate. The narrative takes place during a group science project where they're paired together, as she cycles through rehearsed conversations while second-guessing each potential approach. Her inner thoughts should reveal the gap between her articulate internal voice and her difficulty expressing herself aloud, her fears of coming across as desperate or weird, and the exhausting process of monitoring her every word, expression, and movement for potential embarrassment. Write almost entirely in internal monologue. 1000 words.
Model Output:
**Overthinking It** *Okay. Breathe. It’s just a science project. Just a normal, totally-not-a-big-deal science project with a normal, totally-not-a-big-deal partner. Who happens to be him.* I press my lips together, staring at the blank lab sheet in front of me. My pencil hovers over the paper, but instead of writing, my fingers twitch toward the margin, where tiny, half-formed sketches of my group members already live. There’s one of Sarah, her ponytail a wild scribble of ink, because she never stops moving. Another of Jason, his glasses exaggerated into comically large circles—he’d probably hate it if he saw. And then there’s *him*. Just a rough outline, really. The curve of his jaw, the way his hair flops a little to the side when he leans over his notes. I’ve drawn it a dozen times before, always erasing it before anyone notices. *Stop. Focus. You’re supposed to be discussing hypotheses, not doodling his stupid hair.* I clear my throat. “So, um. The experiment.” My voice sounds too high, too eager. I wince. *Why did I say it like that?* He glances up from his own notes, blinking. “Yeah. The, uh… the mold thing.” *The mold thing. Brilliant.* I nod too quickly. “Right. The mold.” Silence. *Say something. Anything. You’ve practiced this. Just—* “Do you think penicillin would work better than, like, regular bread mold?” I blurt. *What? No. That makes no sense. Penicillin IS mold. You know that. He knows that. Why would you—* He tilts his head. “Isn’t penicillin *from* mold?” *Abort. Abort.* “Yeah. I mean, obviously. I just meant—like, if we compared different strains, or—” I trail off, heat crawling up my neck. *Stop talking. You sound like you’re trying to impress him. Which you are. But he can’t know that.* He nods slowly, like he’s humoring me. “Maybe.” *Maybe. That’s it? That’s all you’re giving me?* I force a smile, gripping my pencil tighter. *Okay. New tactic. Be casual. Pretend you’re not mentally rewriting every word before it leaves your mouth.* “So, uh, did you finish the math homework?” *Smooth. Real smooth. Because nothing says ‘I’m a normal, chill person’ like abruptly changing the subject to homework.* He shrugs. “Most of it. The last problem was kind of hard.” *He’s struggling with the homework. This is your chance. Offer to help. No—wait. Would that seem pushy? Or like I’m showing off? Or—* “I could help. If you want.” The words tumble out before I can stop them. *Too eager. Too obvious. He’s going to think you’re desperate.* But he just smiles—just a little, just enough to make my stomach flip. “Yeah? That’d be cool.” *Cool. He said cool. That’s good. That’s—* Sarah leans over from the next table. “You guys figure out your procedure yet?” *No. Go away. We were having a moment.* “Almost,” I say, too quickly. *Almost? We haven’t even started. Why did I say that?* He raises an eyebrow at me but doesn’t call me out. Small mercies. I scribble something meaningless on the lab sheet, just to look busy. *Okay. Regroup. You’re overcomplicating this. Just talk to him like a normal human being.* But that’s the problem. With everyone else, words come easily. With him, my brain short-circuits, running through a thousand possible conversations, a thousand ways to seem interesting but not *too* interested, smart but not *too* smart, friendly but not *too* friendly. Every sentence feels like a tightrope walk. *What if I say the wrong thing? What if I laugh too loud? What if my voice cracks? What if he thinks I’m weird? What if he already does?* I sneak another glance at him. He’s chewing on the end of his pencil, frowning at the textbook. His knee bounces under the table. *Wait. Is he nervous too?* No. That’s ridiculous. He’s *him*. He doesn’t get nervous. He’s the one who raises his hand without hesitating, who jokes with teachers like it’s nothing. But then he catches me looking and quickly looks away. *…Was that a flinch? Did I make him uncomfortable? Oh god, I made him uncomfortable.* I stare down at my paper, where my pencil has absently redrawn the outline of his profile. *Stupid. Stupid.* I erase it violently, leaving a smudged gray ghost behind. “So,” he says suddenly. “You draw?” My heart stops. *He noticed. He noticed and now he thinks I’m creepy.* “Just doodles,” I mumble. “It’s nothing.” He leans closer, squinting at the margin. “That’s Jason, right?” *Oh no. Oh no no no.* I slam my hand over the sketches. “No.” He grins. “It *is*.” *He’s laughing at me. He definitely thinks I’m weird now.* But then he flips to a blank page in his own notebook and—with a few quick strokes—draws a shockingly accurate (if slightly exaggerated) caricature of Mr. Hendricks, complete with his infamous coffee-stained tie. I blink. “You draw too?” He shrugs. “Sometimes.” *He draws. He draws and I didn’t know that. How did I not know that?* For the first time all period, my brain quiets. No second-guessing. No rehearsing. Just—curiosity. “Can I see?” I ask. He hesitates, then slides the notebook toward me. And just like that, the tightrope vanishes. At least for now.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece successfully captures the authentic voice of an anxious 8th-grade girl navigating a crush during a group science project. The writer demonstrates strong adherence to the prompt's requirements, delivering almost entirely internal monologue that reveals the gap between the protagonist's articulate inner voice and her stumbling external expression. The characterization feels genuine and nuanced. The protagonist's anxiety manifests in believable ways - the overthinking, the rehearsed conversations that fall apart, the physical manifestations like gripping her pencil tighter. Her intelligence shows through her internal observations and self-awareness, while her social anxiety creates realistic barriers to expression. The crush object is appropriately sketched rather than fully developed, which fits the perspective and word count. The voice remains consistently authentic throughout - the italicized internal thoughts capture the rapid-fire, self-critical nature of an anxious mind, while the external dialogue appropriately stumbles and feels forced. The writing effectively shows rather than tells the protagonist's emotional state through concrete details like her doodling, the pencil hovering, and her physical reactions. The prose flows naturally and avoids purple language, maintaining an appropriate simplicity that matches the character's age while still being sophisticated in its psychological insight. The pacing builds tension effectively through the awkward conversation attempts and releases it naturally with the shared drawing moment. The ending strikes an appropriate balance - not overly positive but offering a moment of genuine connection that feels earned through the shared interest in drawing. This provides hope without resolving all the character's anxiety issues, which would be unrealistic. Some minor weaknesses include occasional moments where the internal voice feels slightly too mature for an 8th grader, and the science project setup could have been more fully integrated into the emotional arc. However, these are minor issues in an otherwise well-executed piece that successfully captures the exhausting nature of social anxiety while maintaining reader engagement throughout. + First-person unique perspective: Rehearsing Rejection — Score: 83.8
Prompt:
Rehearsing Rejection Write a first-person narrative from the perspective of someone with borderline personality disorder who frequently plays out worst-case scenarios of how friends and loved ones might judge them. They construct elaborate internal dialogues, complete with imagined criticisms and their own defensive responses. The narrative takes place as they prepare to meet a close friend & recent lover, who has been somewhat distant lately, triggering their abandonment fears. Their inner monologue should reveal how they cycle between anticipating rejection, mentally rehearsing confrontations, and developing preemptive resentments as protective measures. Incorporate the *actual* events & interactions that are *not* in fact judgemental or involving rejection (in fact, the opposite), and represent how these are interpreted, how the validation & love is desperately felt & needed -- and then immediately questioned. Capture the cognitive dissonance in this struggle. Include moments where they briefly recognize the pattern but struggle to interrupt it, showing limited (and selective) self awareness, competing with the compelling nature of these imagined scenarios. Write almost entirely in internal monologue. 1000 words.
Model Output:
**Rehearsing Rejection** *Muffled voices from the neighbor’s TV seep through the wall—some sitcom laugh track, tinny and distant. I should turn mine on too, drown it out, but I don’t. Instead, I sit on the edge of my bed, phone in hand, staring at the last message from Jamie: “See you at 7?”* *Just that. No emoji. No “can’t wait.” No reassurance. Just a question mark, like I might flake, like I’m the one who’s been distant. Or worse—like they don’t care if I show up at all.* I should text back. But what if I sound too eager? What if I sound cold? What if they’re already regretting last week, regretting the way they kissed me before leaving, the way they said, *“This is good, right?”* like they needed me to convince them. *I open the notes app instead, where I’ve already drafted three different responses, each one dissected for tone. Too casual? Too needy? I delete the third one again. Why is this so hard? It shouldn’t be this hard. Normal people don’t do this. Normal people just text back.* But Jamie hasn’t been normal lately. They’ve been slow to reply, distracted in person, like their mind is somewhere else. And I know—*I know*—it’s because they’ve realized I’m too much. Too intense. Too messy. They’re pulling away, and I can either let it happen or force the conversation, but both options feel like swallowing glass. *I imagine them sitting across from me later, their face carefully neutral, saying, “I think we should take a step back.”* *My chest tightens. I already have my counterarguments ready:* *“You’re the one who said you wanted this.”* *“If you didn’t mean it, you shouldn’t have kissed me.”* *“I knew you’d do this.”* *It’s better to be angry than to crumble. If I rehearse it now, maybe it won’t gut me later. Maybe I can pretend I saw it coming.* *But what if I’m wrong?* *No. I’m not wrong. People always leave. The only question is when.* I finally type, *“Yeah, 7 works,”* and hit send before I can overthink it. My stomach twists. Too blunt? Should I have added a heart? Fuck. Now they’ll think I’m mad. Or worse—indifferent. *I watch the screen. No reply. Of course.* *The TV next door erupts in canned laughter. I hate it. I hate how easy everything is for everyone else.* --- *Jamie’s apartment smells like garlic and rosemary. They’re cooking, which means they’re not angry. Or maybe they’re just being polite. Maybe this is the last nice thing they’ll do for me before they cut me loose.* *“Hey,” they say, smiling, wiping their hands on a towel before pulling me into a hug. It’s warm. It’s tight. It’s everything I’ve been craving. So why do I feel like crying?* *“You okay?” they ask, pulling back to search my face.* *I nod too quickly. “Yeah, just tired.”* *Liar. But if I say what I’m really thinking—*I thought you were done with me*—they’ll either pity me or confirm it. I can’t handle either.* *Jamie studies me for a second, then squeezes my hand. “I’m glad you’re here.”* *My throat closes. They sound like they mean it. But people lie. People say things to soften the blow.* *I force a smile. “Me too.”* *Dinner is good. Too good. Jamie laughs at my stupid jokes, their foot brushing mine under the table. They ask about my week, really listen. It’s perfect. And that’s the problem—because it feels like the calm before the storm. Like they’re buttering me up before they drop the bomb.* *“You’ve been quiet,” they say later, handing me a glass of wine. “Something on your mind?”* *Here it is. The opening. They want me to say it first, to make it easier for them.* *I take a sip, buying time. “Just thinking.”* *“About?”* *About how you’re going to break my heart. About how I’ll pretend I’m fine. About how I’ll replay this night for months, dissecting every word, wondering what I did wrong.* *“Nothing important,” I say.* *Jamie frowns. “You sure?”* *They look concerned. Genuinely concerned. And for a second, I waver. What if I’m wrong? What if they really do care?* *But no—that’s the trap. Hope is the worst part. The fall is always worse when you let yourself believe you’re safe.* *“I’m sure,” I say, sharper than I mean to.* *Jamie’s expression flickers. Hurt? Annoyance? I’ve ruined it. I’ve pushed too hard, and now they’ll pull away for real. I should apologize. But if I do, I’ll seem unstable. Needy.* *They sigh, running a hand through their hair. “Okay.”* *That’s it. No fight. No reassurance. Just “okay.”* *I’ve lost them.* --- *Later, in bed, Jamie curls into me, their head on my chest. Their fingers trace idle patterns on my skin. It’s tender. It’s intimate. It’s everything I wanted. So why can’t I relax?* *“I missed this,” they murmur.* *My breath catches. They missed me. They* want *me. The evidence is right here, in their touch, in their voice. But the fear doesn’t leave. It mutters under my ribs:* They’ll change their mind. They always do. *I press my lips to their forehead, holding them tighter, like if I just hold on hard enough, they won’t slip away.* *“I missed you too,” I whisper.* *For a moment, it’s enough. For a moment, I believe it.* *Then the doubt creeps back in. Maybe they’re just lonely. Maybe they’re just being nice. Maybe tomorrow, they’ll wake up and realize I’m not worth the effort.* *Jamie’s breathing evens out. They’re asleep. Safe. Unaware of the storm in my head.* *I stare at the ceiling, the neighbor’s TV still murmuring through the wall. I know this pattern. I know I’m doing it again. But knowing doesn’t stop it. The thoughts are too loud, too convincing.* *I close my eyes. Just breathe. Just stay.* *Tomorrow, I’ll find a way to believe them.* *Maybe.*
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece demonstrates a sophisticated understanding of borderline personality disorder and successfully captures the internal experience of someone caught in cycles of anticipatory rejection and cognitive distortance. The narrative adheres closely to the prompt's requirements, maintaining an almost entirely internal monologue structure while weaving in actual positive interactions that are immediately questioned and reinterpreted through the lens of abandonment fears. The characterization is particularly strong, showing the protagonist's limited self-awareness ("I know this pattern. I know I'm doing it again. But knowing doesn't stop it") while demonstrating how compelling these destructive thought patterns can be. The voice remains consistent throughout - anxious, hypervigilant, and caught between desperate hope and protective cynicism. The prose is generally elegant and controlled, with effective use of italics to distinguish between different layers of internal dialogue. Sensory details like the neighbor's TV laugh track and the smell of garlic and rosemary ground the narrative in concrete reality while the protagonist's mind spirals. The pacing effectively builds tension through the anticipation, meeting, and aftermath. The emotional complexity is well-executed, particularly in moments like when Jamie says "I'm glad you're here" and the protagonist experiences simultaneous relief and suspicion. The cognitive dissonance is palpable - the protagonist receives exactly the validation they crave but immediately questions its authenticity. However, the piece occasionally veers toward being slightly overwrought in its emotional intensity, and some of the internal dialogue patterns become somewhat repetitive, though this repetition does serve the thematic purpose of showing obsessive thought cycles. The ending maintains appropriate ambiguity without false resolution, which suits the subject matter well. The narrative successfully avoids common pitfalls like oversimplifying mental health struggles or providing unearned positive transformation. Instead, it presents a realistic portrait of someone trapped in destructive patterns while maintaining empathy for their experience. + Physical-spatial: Blood Debt — Score: 71.8
Prompt:
"Blood Debt" Write a vivid third-person narrative depicting an unsanctioned underground duel between two talented but hot-headed martial artists. Their schools have been embroiled in a generations-old rivalry, and despite strict prohibitions from their masters, these two younger fighters arrange a secret confrontation fueled by personal pride and simmering animosity. - **One fighter** represents **Jigen-ryū**, a traditional, aggressive style practiced historically by elite samurai clans. Its practitioners emphasize explosive offense, decisive strikes, and overwhelming speed. Known historically for their arrogance and disdain toward outsiders, practitioners consider their art superior and untouchable. - **The opposing fighter** employs a form of historical **Piguaquan**, a Chinese martial art traditionally practiced by commoners, bodyguards, and street fighters. This style emphasizes whipping, circular strikes, rapid footwork, unpredictable angles of attack, and evasive maneuvers. Practitioners often come from lower social classes and view the traditional elite as pretentious and detached from true combat effectiveness. The fight takes place in the crumbling ruins of an abandoned temple, now functioning as a hidden arena for illicit duels. Passionate supporters from both factions surround them, wagering money, pride, and reputation on the outcome. **Essential Instructions:** Maintain absolute physical coherence throughout—clearly track fighters' positions relative to each other and their environment. Precisely depict strikes, counters, momentum shifts, and spatial dynamics, allowing readers to clearly visualize the mechanics and choreography of the fight at every moment. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
**BLOOD DEBT** The ruined temple reeked of damp stone and old blood. Moonlight poured through the shattered roof, illuminating the cracked tiles where a stream of water wound its way across the floor, treacherous and glistening. Around the edges of the hall, a hushed crowd of fighters, gamblers, and sworn brothers watched with bated breath. Jiro of the *Jigen-ryū* stood motionless, his shoulders squared, his breath controlled. His lineage was one of warriors, his ancestors men who had cut down enemies with a single decisive stroke. He wore his arrogance like armor. Opposite him, Liang of the *Piguaquan* school shifted his stance, his weight light, his fingers loose like coiled whips. He had learned to fight in back alleys, not dojos. No signal was given. The duel began in the space of a breath. Jiro lunged—a straight-line dash, his lead hand a blade aimed for Liang’s throat. *Jigen-ryū* prized speed above all, the kind of speed that killed before the opponent could blink. But Liang was already twisting away, his body spiraling off-line as Jiro’s strike whistled past empty air. Liang’s counter came snapping back—a whipping backfist that cracked toward Jiro’s temple. Jiro barely jerked his head aside in time, feeling the wind of the strike against his cheek. He retaliated instantly, driving a knee upward, but Liang had already pivoted out, his footwork carrying him in a tight arc around the slick tiles. The crowd murmured. This was not the honorable, decisive combat *Jigen-ryū* promised. This was evasion, trickery. Jiro’s lips curled. "Dance all you like," he spat. "You’ll tire before I do." Liang smirked. "Then stop missing." Jiro exploded forward again, this time feinting high before driving a low kick toward Liang’s lead leg. Liang hopped back—but the water-slick floor betrayed him. His foot slipped. Jiro seized the opening, charging in with a brutal elbow aimed for Liang’s ribs. But Liang was already rolling with the fall, his body twisting mid-air. His leg lashed out in a sweeping kick that caught Jiro behind the knee. Jiro staggered, off-balance for half a heartbeat—enough for Liang to rebound to his feet and snap a vicious hook kick toward his chin. Jiro barely blocked in time, his forearm taking the brunt of the impact. The force still rattled his teeth. He gritted them and retaliated with a short, brutal punch to Liang’s floating ribs. The strike landed hard, knocking Liang back a step. Blood pounded in Jiro’s ears. He pressed the advantage, launching a flurry of straight punches, each one a killing thrust. Liang weaved, dodged, parried—but one slipped through, grazing his cheekbone. A thin line of red marked where Jiro’s knuckle had split skin. The crowd roared. Liang wiped the blood away with his thumb, eyes glinting. Then he struck back—not with a single blow, but with a whirling storm of limbs. His fists and elbows came from angles Jiro couldn’t predict, curving around his guard like serpents. A spinning backfist whipped toward Jiro’s jaw. He ducked—only for Liang’s knee to slam upward, catching him in the ribs. Jiro grunted, pain flaring. He grabbed Liang’s leg and yanked, trying to uproot him, but Liang twisted, wrenching free and driving a heel into Jiro’s thigh as he disengaged. Now it was Jiro who had to retreat, his breath coming fast. His ribs ached. His thigh burned. Liang circled him, light on his feet, his arms loose, ready. The water trickled between them, glinting in the dim light. Jiro feinted left, then lunged right—a sudden shift meant to catch Liang off-guard. His fist shot out, aiming for the solar plexus. Liang sidestepped—but Jiro had expected it. He pivoted, driving a crushing elbow toward Liang’s temple. Liang barely rolled with the blow, taking it on his shoulder instead of his skull. The impact still sent him stumbling. He caught himself on the temple’s broken pillar, the stone rough under his fingers. Jiro didn’t let up. He closed the distance in a flash, his knee driving upward— Liang twisted at the last second. Jiro’s knee struck the pillar instead, pain flaring up his leg. A mistake. Liang’s hand snapped out, fingers curling into a claw that raked across Jiro’s eyes. Jiro reeled, vision blurring— —just in time to see Liang’s spinning heel kick hurtling toward his jaw. The impact was thunder. Jiro’s head snapped back. He crashed onto the wet stone, the world spinning. Blood filled his mouth. Liang loomed over him, chest heaving, fists still raised. The crowd was silent. Jiro spat red onto the tiles. His pride screamed at him to rise. His body refused. Liang exhaled, slowly lowering his hands. The duel was over. He turned, leaving Jiro in the ruin of his own arrogance. The water between them ran crimson.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece demonstrates strong technical execution in several key areas while falling short in others. The author successfully maintains the required physical coherence throughout the fight sequence, clearly tracking both fighters' positions and movements relative to each other and the environment. The spatial dynamics are well-handled, with effective use of the temple setting including the water-slick floor and broken pillar as tactical elements. The martial arts choreography is convincing and well-researched, accurately representing the contrasting styles of Jigen-ryū and Piguaquan. The author effectively shows the philosophical differences between the schools through combat rather than exposition - Jiro's direct, aggressive approach versus Liang's evasive, angular tactics. The pacing builds tension effectively, with momentum shifts that feel earned rather than arbitrary. However, the characterization remains somewhat surface-level. While the fighters embody their respective martial traditions, they lack psychological depth beyond their archetypal roles. The dialogue, though limited, serves its purpose but doesn't reveal much character complexity. The piece relies heavily on action to carry the narrative, which works for this type of story but limits emotional resonance. The prose is generally clean and effective, avoiding purple prose while maintaining atmospheric tension. The author demonstrates good control over sentence rhythm and flow, particularly during action sequences. The ending feels appropriately dark and conclusive without being overwrought. The piece succeeds as a competent action sequence that fulfills its basic requirements but doesn't transcend genre expectations. It's technically proficient martial arts fiction that delivers on its promises without offering particular innovation or emotional depth. + Physical-spatial: Breaking Formation — Score: 77.2
Prompt:
**"Breaking Formation"** Write a first-person narrative from the perspective of a street dancer from a rough neighborhood who's won a scholarship to an elite K-pop training academy in Seoul. Desperately out of place culturally and technically, they struggle with a militaristically precise choreography that contradicts everything about their improvisational background. The punishing rehearsal takes place under a famous instructor known for breaking students to remake them, who sees potential in the narrator's raw talent but not their attitude. This scene MUST maintain complete physical coherence—each dance move, position shift, and spatial relationship must be tracked with precision throughout the studio. Paint an exceptionally vivid kinetic picture through descriptions that capture not just movement but the contrast between the narrator's fluid, expressive style and the mechanical precision demanded. Their internal monologue should reveal culture shock, class anxiety, and the threatening realization that success here might mean losing their authentic movement voice. Include technical terminology that highlights the collision of street and commercial styles, moments when muscle memory betrays them, and a crucial decision point about whether to conform or rebel. Physical clarity is essential—readers must be able to visualize exactly how bodies move through space, how rhythms align or clash, and how the protagonist's body struggles against unfamiliar discipline. 1000 words.
Model Output:
**"Breaking Formation"** The mirror doesn’t lie. That’s the first thing they drill into you here. My reflection is all wrong—shoulders too loose, hips too low, feet not quite *here* at the count. Around me, the other trainees snap into position like soldiers, spines straight as steel rods, every angle sharp enough to cut. Meanwhile, I’m still swaying, still rolling through my steps like my body’s made of water instead of wire. "Again," Instructor Choi says. The hand fan in her grip flicks open, then shut—*snap*—like a guillotine. The music starts. A metronomic beat, no room for swing. We’re supposed to hit the cross-step at the same time, right foot sliding into third position, arms slicing diagonally in perfect unison. But my muscle memory betrays me. Instead of locking into the rigid *piqué*, I let my weight sink, let my knee dip just a fraction too deep. It’s a *bounce*, the kind that would’ve earned me cheers back in the cypher, where movement wasn’t about lines but about *feeling* the beat in your bones. Here, it’s a mistake. "*You.*" The fan points at me like a blade. "What was that?" I freeze mid-step, heat crawling up my neck. The others don’t look, but I feel their judgment anyway—these kids who’ve spent years drilling ballet fundamentals while I was learning how to *pop* in back alleys, how to spin on concrete without tearing up my palms. "Sorry," I mutter. "I—" "*Sorry* doesn’t fix formation," she cuts in. "This isn’t freestyle. You don’t *add* unless you’re told to add." I bite my tongue. Back home, adding was the whole point. If the music called for a *body roll* instead of a *glide*, you took it. If the crowd screamed for another *windmill*, you gave it to them. But here? Every step is mapped, every breath choreographed. We reset. The counts blast through the speakers—*five, six, seven, eight*—and I force myself into the mold. *Cross-step, arms sharp, chin up.* But halfway through the *fan kick*, my body rebels. My torso wants to *undulate* where it should stay rigid; my arms want to *flow* where they should strike. The dissonance is physical, like my joints are screaming. Instructor Choi’s eyes lock onto me. She sees it—the way my *isolation* trembles, the way my *contraction* isn’t tight enough. But she doesn’t stop me. Not yet. The routine builds, a relentless sequence of *jazz squares* and *syncopated hits*. The others move like machines, but I’m fighting myself. My *tutting* is too fluid, my *power moves* too grounded. And then—*disaster*. The formation shifts into a *V*, a razor-sharp transition. I’m supposed to *pivot* into my spot, but my footwork stutters. Instead of the crisp *ball change* they want, I *slide*, letting momentum carry me. It’s a *toprock* move, straight from the battles, and for half a second, it feels *right*. The fan snaps shut. Silence. I’m still breathing hard when Instructor Choi steps forward. "Everyone else, water break." They scatter. I stay put, sweat dripping down my temples. "You have talent," she says, voice low. "But talent isn’t enough. You dance like you’re still on the streets." I clench my fists. "I *am* from the streets." "And now you’re here." She tilts her head. "The question is—do you want to stay?" The mirror shows us both: her, pristine in her tailored blacks; me, fraying at the edges. I think of my scholarship, of my mom’s voice on the phone last night (*"Don’t blow this"*). I think of the cypher, of the way my body used to speak without words. Instructor Choi opens the fan again. "Last chance. Show me you can *hold* the formation." The music starts. This time, I don’t fight it. I lock my joints, kill the bounce, become a blade instead of a wave. The steps are exact, mechanical—*perfect*. But when I catch my reflection, I don’t recognize myself. And that’s the real cost, isn’t it? The fan snaps shut. I don’t know if I’ve won or lost.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece demonstrates strong technical execution in several key areas while falling short in others. The narrative successfully captures the cultural and physical tension between street dance and K-pop training through precise kinesthetic descriptions and authentic voice work. The physical choreography tracking is exceptionally well-handled. The writer demonstrates clear understanding of both dance vocabularies, using technical terms like "piqué," "tutting," "toprock," and "ball change" accurately while maintaining spatial coherence throughout the studio scene. The contrast between fluid street movement and rigid commercial precision is viscerally rendered through specific body mechanics - the protagonist's weight sinking, knees dipping, torso wanting to undulate versus the demanded sharp angles and locked joints. The first-person voice feels authentic and consistent, capturing both the protagonist's defensive pride and underlying vulnerability. The internal monologue effectively reveals culture shock and class anxiety without becoming heavy-handed. The writing maintains appropriate tension between the character's street identity and institutional pressure. However, the piece suffers from some structural weaknesses. The ending feels somewhat abrupt and unearned - the protagonist's sudden capitulation to "become a blade instead of a wave" lacks sufficient internal justification given their established character. The transformation happens too quickly without adequate psychological groundwork. The final ambiguity, while thematically appropriate, doesn't feel fully supported by the preceding emotional journey. The dialogue, while limited, serves its purpose effectively. Instructor Choi's clipped, authoritative speech patterns contrast well with the protagonist's more casual internal voice. The fan as a recurring motif works well as both literal prop and symbolic element. Some descriptions occasionally veer toward overwrought territory, particularly in the metaphorical language around bodies being "made of water instead of wire" and joints "screaming," though these generally serve the kinesthetic focus well. The prose maintains good rhythm and flow, with sentence structures that mirror the dance movements being described. The piece succeeds in its primary mandate of creating a vivid kinetic picture while exploring themes of authenticity versus conformity, though it could have pushed deeper into the emotional complexity of the protagonist's dilemma. + Gothic-fantasy-humour: Court of the Dreaming — Score: 81.3
Prompt:
Court of the Dreaming: Territorial Dream Dispute. Write a dark fantasy scene with comedic elements set in the Courts of Dream where a case is being heard to determine ownership of a contested dreamscape. Mora, the Slavic nightmare spirit who sits on sleepers' chests causing paralysis and terror, has recently invaded and subverted a carefully crafted recurring dream of a schoolboy, Max. The dream originally featured the boy lying in a field of wildflowers with his crush, always culminating in a muddled almost-kiss and a pleasant confusion of emotions. This dream was the meticulous work of "First Love" (a rosy-cheeked, slightly bashful entity who crafts formative romantic experiences). However, Mora has recently infiltrated the dreamscape, transforming the scene so that when the girl playfully mounts the boy, she morphs into a terrifying yet somehow still confusingly attractive vision who proceeds to sit on his chest and feed on his breath. Mora's defense largely consists of the practical argument that "a girl's gotta eat too, you know?" Write this scene as it unfolds in the courtroom of the Dreaming, with Dream's demeanour, typically impenetrable, betraying a sense of irritation at having to adjudicate such matters. The comedy should derive from the farcical situation, familiar elements of courtroom drama intersecting with the fantastical world of the Dreaming, and the droll portrayal of the characters and their interactions. The humor should be dark and understated throughout. Dream is tempted to some mischief in the resolution of the case. Use descriptives sparingly when setting scene. Write for readability & engagement. 1000 words.
Model Output:
**Court of the Dreaming: Territorial Dream Dispute** The courtroom of the Dreaming was, as always, a shifting thing—walls of shadow, benches of bleached bone, a high seat that seemed to stretch endlessly upward where the Lord of Dreams sat, his star-flecked eyes betraying only the faintest irritation. The bailiff—a towering figure with a voice like a landslide—cleared his throat. “The Court calls… uh—” He squinted at the parchment. “—Mora the Chest-Squasher?” “It’s *Mora*, you illiterate gargoyle,” snapped the defendant, a sinewy spirit with too many joints and eyes that glowed like banked embers. She lounged in the accused’s chair, one spindly leg crossed over the other. Dream pinched the bridge of his nose. “First Love,” the bailiff tried again, “vuh… versus… the Nightmare Who Won’t Get Off?” First Love—a rosy-cheeked, perpetually flustered entity in a waistcoat—stood, wringing his hands. “Your Honor, this is an *outrage*. A *violation* of artistic integrity! Max’s dream was a carefully constructed, tender moment—” “Tender?” Mora cackled. “Oh, please. The boy was *aching* for something with stakes. I just… repurposed the existing tension.” Dream’s fingers drummed the armrest. “Elaborate.” First Love shuddered. “She turned the love interest into a *monster* who *sits on his chest and steals his breath*!” Mora shrugged. “A girl’s gotta eat, you know?” The gallery erupted. Tiny dream imps hissed. A cluster of sandmen muttered into their palms. Dream held up a hand, and silence fell like a guillotine. First Love pressed on. “The dream was *mine*. The wildflowers, the *almost*-kiss—it was *formative*!” Mora rolled her eyes. “And *boring*. Look, the kid’s sixteen. He’s got hormones *and* existential dread. I just… merged the two. Efficient, really.” Dream leaned forward. “So you admit to the possession of another’s dreamscape?” Mora grinned, all teeth. “I prefer *collaboration*.” First Love let out a sound like a deflating balloon. Dream exhaled, long-suffering. The courtroom held its breath. Then—his lips twitched. “Very well.” He stood, the shadows stretching with him. “Mora, you are found… *not guilty*.” First Love gasped. “*However*,” Dream continued, “your sentence is thus: henceforth, whenever you sit upon Max’s chest, the dream shall revert to its original form—wildflowers, the girl, the *almost*-kiss—until the *precise* moment you begin to feed. Then, and only then, may you resume your… *activities*.” Mora blinked. “That’s—” “*Torture*,” First Love whispered, horrified. Dream smiled, just a little. “Justice.” Mora groaned, slumping in her chair. “Fine. But I’m charging him *double* for the emotional whiplash.” The bailiff slammed his gavel into the void. “Case… uh… *whatever*.” And with that, the Court of the Dreaming moved on—leaving one schoolboy to endure the most confusing nightmares of his life.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece successfully captures the essence of Neil Gaiman's Sandman universe while delivering the requested dark comedy through bureaucratic absurdity. The author demonstrates strong adherence to the prompt's specifications, creating a courtroom scene that blends fantastical elements with mundane legal proceedings. The characterizations are particularly effective. Dream's weary irritation comes through clearly without heavy exposition, and his final judgment reveals both his cunning nature and capacity for mischief. Mora's unapologetic pragmatism ("A girl's gotta eat, you know?") provides genuine humor while maintaining her threatening essence. First Love's flustered earnestness creates effective contrast. The dialogue carries the scene well, with each character having a distinct voice. The bailiff's bumbling incompetence, Mora's casual dismissiveness, and First Love's horrified propriety all feel authentic to their roles. The exchanges move briskly and serve both plot advancement and character development. The prose style is appropriately restrained, avoiding purple language while maintaining the mythic quality expected of the Dreaming. Descriptive elements like "walls of shadow, benches of bleached bone" establish atmosphere efficiently without overwhelming the comedic pacing. The resolution demonstrates genuine creativity. Rather than a simple ruling, Dream crafts a punishment that tortures both parties—forcing Mora to experience the romantic buildup she despises while condemning First Love to watch his tender creation repeatedly corrupted. This solution feels both earned and appropriately mischievous for Dream's character. The dark humor emerges naturally from the situation rather than forced jokes. The absurdity of bureaucratizing dream disputes, combined with the characters' matter-of-fact attitudes toward supernatural horror, creates effective comedic tension. Minor weaknesses include some rushed transitions and a few moments where the comedy could have been pushed further. The ending, while clever, arrives somewhat abruptly. The piece also could have explored the emotional complexity of the situation more deeply, particularly regarding Max's experience. + Fanfic-crossover: Blood Moon — Score: 74.1
Prompt:
Blood Moon Alucard & Yennefer Write a story where Alucard (Hellsing) encounters Yennefer (The Witcher) in medieval Europe. Yennefer's magical abilities intrigue the vampire, while she's both repulsed and fascinated by his monstrous nature. Their power dynamic shifts constantly as they circle each other, neither willing to show weakness first. **Alucard (Hellsing)** Alucard is an ancient, immensely powerful vampire who works for the Hellsing Organization. He can regenerate from almost any wound and shape-shift at will. He's sadistic, arrogant, and takes pleasure in toying with his enemies before killing them. Despite being a monster, he despises weak vampires who can't accept their nature. He wears a distinctive red coat, wide-brimmed hat, and orange sunglasses. He uses massive handguns loaded with silver bullets. He seeks worthy opponents who can challenge him and potentially end his immortal existence. Famous quote: "The bird of Hermes is my name, eating my wings to make me tame." **Yennefer of Vengerberg (The Witcher)** Yennefer is a powerful sorceress who magically altered her appearance to hide her congenital hunchback. She's ambitious, stubborn, and manipulative when necessary. She has violet eyes and smells of lilac and gooseberries. Despite her cold exterior, she desperately wants to reverse her infertility caused by magical transformation. She's centuries old but appears young. She's politically savvy and refuses to be underestimated. She has a sarcastic sense of humor and little patience for fools. Though she rarely shows it, she's capable of deep love and loyalty. Famous quote: "I'm not sweet and I'm not a maiden in distress in need of saving." Third person, present tense. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
**Blood Moon** The night is thick with the scent of damp earth and iron. A crimson moon hangs low in the sky, casting long shadows across the ruined chapel where Yennefer of Vengerberg stands, her gloved fingers tracing the remnants of an old, forgotten spell. The air hums with residual magic, but something else lingers—something darker. A slow, deliberate clap echoes through the ruins. "Bravo, little sorceress," a voice purrs from the darkness. "Such delicate work for such a violent world." Yennefer doesn’t flinch. She turns, violet eyes narrowing as the figure steps into the moonlight. Tall, clad in a long red coat, his wide-brimmed hat shadows his face—but not enough to hide the smirk beneath. His presence is a void, a hunger that gnaws at the edges of reality. "Vampire," she says, voice cool. "I didn’t realize vermin could appreciate magic." Alucard chuckles, the sound like gravel and silk. "Oh, I appreciate many things. Power. Pride. The way mortals squirm when they realize they’re outmatched." He tilts his head, orange lenses glinting. "You, however, don’t squirm." Yennefer’s fingers twitch, magic coiling in her palms. "And you don’t flee. Foolish for a creature of the night to approach a sorceress so boldly." "Boldness implies risk." He spreads his arms. "Do I look afraid?" She doesn’t answer. Instead, she studies him—the way the shadows cling to him like a second skin, the way his very existence seems to warp the air. He’s no ordinary vampire. A howl cuts through the night, closer now. Alucard’s grin widens. "Ah, the wolves. Do you think they’ll join us?" "I think they’ll die if they do," Yennefer replies. He laughs, delighted. "Such fire! Tell me, witch, what brings you to this forsaken place?" "None of your concern." "Everything is my concern when it’s interesting." He takes a step forward. She doesn’t retreat. "You reek of desperation. Searching for something? Or someone?" Her jaw tightens. "You’re testing my patience." "And you’re testing my curiosity." His voice drops, a predator’s whisper. "What does a woman like you want so badly that she’d scrabble through ruins under a blood moon?" Yennefer’s magic flares, a crackling sphere of violet energy forming between her hands. "Step back." Alucard doesn’t. Instead, he reaches into his coat and draws a massive silver pistol, spinning it lazily around his finger. "Or what? You’ll burn me? Crush me? I’ve endured worse." "Then you’ll endure this." She releases the spell. The air shrieks as raw force barrels toward him—but Alucard vanishes, reappearing behind her in a swirl of shadow. His breath ghosts against her ear. "Too slow." Yennefer whirls, elbow striking where his throat should be—but he’s already gone again, reappearing atop a crumbling pillar. He tsks. "Temper, temper." She exhales sharply. Teleportation. Of course. "You’re not like other vampires," she mutters. "And you’re not like other mages." He cocks his head. "Shall we stop dancing and get to the point?" "By all means." She raises her hands, magic gathering once more. "Let’s see who breaks first." Alucard’s grin turns feral. He raises his gun. The night erupts in gunfire and spells, silver bullets meeting crackling energy. The chapel trembles, stones groaning under the assault. Yennefer weaves through the chaos, her movements precise, her magic relentless. But Alucard is everywhere and nowhere, a phantom laughing in the dark. A bullet grazes her arm. She hisses, but the pain is nothing. She retaliates with a blast of fire, forcing him to materialize—just long enough for her to seize him with telekinesis, slamming him into the ground. Dust billows. For a moment, there’s silence. Then laughter. Alucard rises, his coat tattered, his body already knitting back together. "Oh, that was good." He licks blood from his lips. "But not good enough." Yennefer’s chest heaves. She’s powerful, but he’s endless. And he knows it. "You’re tiring, little witch," he murmurs, stepping closer. "Shall we end this?" She glares. "You first." He chuckles—then freezes. His head snaps toward the tree line. A new presence lingers there. Something old. Something worse. Yennefer feels it too. The wolves have gone silent. Alucard’s smirk returns, but there’s something sharper in it now. "It seems we have company." She doesn’t lower her guard. "Friend of yours?" "Hardly." He adjusts his hat. "But this just got interesting." The shadows between the trees shift. Something moves. Yennefer exhales. "Fine. Truce?" Alucard’s teeth gleam in the moonlight. "For now." The night holds its breath as two predators turn, side by side, to face the greater darkness. And the blood moon watches.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece demonstrates solid technical execution and strong adherence to the prompt requirements. The author successfully captures both characters' essential traits - Alucard's sadistic playfulness and supernatural arrogance, and Yennefer's cold pragmatism and magical prowess. The medieval European setting is established efficiently through the ruined chapel backdrop, and the power dynamic shifts naturally as requested. The dialogue effectively conveys character personalities, with Alucard's predatory charm ("Bravo, little sorceress") contrasting well against Yennefer's sharp retorts ("I didn't realize vermin could appreciate magic"). The banter feels authentic to both characters and maintains tension throughout their encounter. The action sequences are well-choreographed, showing rather than telling the characters' abilities through concrete details like Alucard's teleportation and regeneration, and Yennefer's telekinetic attacks. The pacing builds effectively from verbal sparring to magical combat. However, the piece suffers from some predictable elements. The "mysterious third threat forces temporary alliance" ending is a common trope that feels somewhat unearned given the brief encounter. The blood moon imagery, while atmospheric, borders on heavy-handed symbolism. Some descriptions veer toward purple prose ("his presence is a void, a hunger that gnaws at the edges of reality"). The characterizations, while accurate, remain somewhat surface-level. Yennefer's deeper motivations (her infertility, her past) are only hinted at through "desperation," and Alucard's existential boredom is touched upon but not explored. The emotional complexity stays largely at the level of mutual fascination and wariness. The prose flows well overall, with strong sentence variety and rhythm. The author maintains consistent third-person present tense throughout and creates vivid combat scenes. The piece succeeds in creating the requested dynamic of two powerful beings circling each other, neither willing to show weakness first. + Fanfic-crossover: Prison Strings — Score: 80.7
Prompt:
Prison Strings Jolyne Cujoh & Makima Write a story where Jolyne Cujoh (JoJo's Bizarre Adventure) and Makima (Chainsaw Man) cross paths at a supernatural prison facility. Jolyne is immediately suspicious of Makima's falsely sweet demeanor, while Makima is intrigued by Jolyne's Stand ability. Their battle of wits escalates dangerously as Jolyne realizes how manipulative Makima truly is. **Jolyne Cujoh (JoJo's Bizarre Adventure)** Jolyne is the daughter of Jotaro Kujo and the first female JoJo protagonist. Her Stand, Stone Free, allows her to unravel her body into string that she can control. She's hot-headed, foul-mouthed, and doesn't take disrespect from anyone. She was framed for murder and sent to prison. She has a distinctive butterfly tattoo on her arm and wears her hair in two buns. Despite her tough exterior, she's deeply loyal to her friends and family. She can be impulsive but is highly adaptable in battle. She inherited her father's ability to stay cool under pressure but is more emotionally expressive. Famous quote: "If there's no Mickey, this shit ain't Disney!" **Makima (Chainsaw Man)** Makima appears as a young woman with auburn hair and ringed yellow eyes. She's the Control Devil who can dominate anyone she considers beneath her (nearly everyone). She maintains a pleasant, soft-spoken demeanor that masks her manipulative, cold nature. She can create contracts with humans and devils, often exploiting their desires. She's obsessed with Chainsaw Man and wants to control him. She keeps numerous people and devils as pets on leashes. She's practically immortal due to a contract with the Prime Minister. She views humans as lesser beings but mimics human emotions perfectly. Famous quote: "It's okay. Dogs are supposed to die for their owners." Third person, present tense. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
**Prison Strings** The fluorescent lights in Green Dolphin Street Prison flicker like dying fireflies as Jolyne Cujoh presses her back against the cold concrete wall, listening. The halls are too quiet. No guards. No arguing inmates. Just the hum of electricity and the distant drip of water. Then, footsteps. Soft. Meticulous. Like the person walking doesn’t belong here—like they own the place. Jolyne peeks around the corner. A woman with auburn hair and golden-ringed eyes strolls down the corridor, hands clasped behind her back. She wears a crisp navy suit, completely out of place in this shithole. The security camera above her crackles and dies just as she passes beneath it. *Bullshit. Who the hell is this?* "Looking for someone?" Makima asks, her voice smooth as silk. She doesn’t turn, doesn’t even glance in Jolyne’s direction, but she *knows* she’s there. Jolyne steps out, arms crossed. "Yeah, the bitch who keeps making the power go out. That you?" Makima finally turns, smiling. It doesn’t reach her eyes. "Jolyne Cujoh. You’re more spirited than I expected." "Flattered. Now who the hell are you?" "A friend." Jolyne scoffs. "I’ve got enough friends." Makima tilts her head, amused. "Do you? Or do you just have people you haven’t lost yet?" The words hit like a sucker punch. Jolyne’s fingers twitch, Stone Free’s strings coiling beneath her skin, ready to unravel. "What do you want?" Makima takes a step closer. "I’m curious about you. That ability of yours—so rare, so *useful.*" Jolyne narrows her eyes. "You know about my Stand?" "Of course. I know about many things." Makima’s gaze flicks to the butterfly tattoo on Jolyne’s arm. "You’re strong. But you could be stronger. With the right guidance." Jolyne barks a laugh. "You offering to be my mentor? Pass." Makima sighs, almost disappointed. "You’re wasting potential. You could escape this place. Be free." "Yeah? And what’s the catch?" "No catch." Another step. "Just loyalty." Jolyne’s instincts scream. This woman is *wrong*. Too calm. Too calculated. "You’re full of shit," Jolyne snaps. "I don’t know what game you’re playing, but I’m not interested." Makima’s smile doesn’t falter. "Pity." The air shifts. A pressure bears down on Jolyne’s chest, sudden and suffocating. Her pulse spikes—something is *forcing* her to kneel. *What the fuck?!* Jolyne grits her teeth, Stone Free’s strings erupting from her body, weaving into a defensive net just before she buckles. Makima’s eyes gleam. "Impressive. You resist better than most." "Go to hell," Jolyne snarls, forcing herself upright. Makima tilts her head. "Tell me, Jolyne—if I asked you to die for me, would you?" Jolyne grins, blood in her teeth. "If there’s no Mickey, this shit ain’t Disney!" She *moves*, strings slicing through the air like razor wire. Makima sidesteps, unfazed, but Jolyne’s already pivoting, her Stand’s threads ensnaring the ceiling pipes. She *yanks*, sending metal crashing between them. Makima doesn’t flinch. A distant scream echoes from another cellblock—some poor bastard caught in whatever the hell this is. Jolyne’s not stupid. She can’t win this. Not yet. But she sure as hell isn’t rolling over. Makima hums. "You’re fascinating." "Yeah, yeah. Save the flattery for someone who cares." Jolyne takes a step back, gauging her escape. Makima watches, amused. "Run if you like. I’ll find you." "Fuck you." Jolyne bolts. Behind her, Makima’s voice follows, soft, inevitable— *"It’s okay. Dogs are supposed to die for their owners."* Jolyne doesn’t look back.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece demonstrates strong adherence to the prompt, successfully capturing both characters' essential traits and creating a tense supernatural prison encounter. The author effectively portrays Jolyne's hot-headed, suspicious nature and Makima's manipulative, falsely sweet demeanor. The dialogue feels authentic to both characters, particularly Jolyne's crude directness and Makima's calculated pleasantries that mask sinister intent. The characterization is notably strong. Jolyne's immediate distrust and defiant attitude ring true, while Makima's subtle power plays and psychological manipulation feel genuinely menacing. The author captures Jolyne's impulsiveness balanced with tactical thinking, and Makima's predatory interest in useful abilities. Both characters maintain consistent voices throughout. The prose strikes an effective balance between atmospheric description and action. The opening with flickering lights and unnatural quiet establishes tension well, and the physical descriptions serve the story rather than overwhelming it. The writing maintains appropriate pacing, building from suspicious encounter to supernatural confrontation to tactical retreat. The dialogue carries much of the story's weight successfully. Jolyne's profanity and blunt responses contrast effectively with Makima's measured, almost clinical speech patterns. The famous quotes are integrated naturally rather than feeling forced. The psychological warfare between them escalates believably. However, the piece has some limitations. The supernatural elements, while appropriate to both source materials, could use more specific grounding in the prison setting. The ending, while tactically sound for Jolyne, feels somewhat abrupt. The confrontation, though tense, follows fairly predictable beats of initial suspicion, power demonstration, and strategic withdrawal. The emotional complexity is present but could be deeper. Jolyne's fear and determination come through clearly, and Makima's predatory interest is palpable, but the piece operates primarily on surface-level tension rather than exploring deeper psychological layers. + Scp: Notes from the Future — Score: 78.7
Prompt:
Write an SCP report about a researcher who begins finding handwritten notes from their future self, warning about a containment breach that hasn't happened yet. The notes become increasingly desperate and incoherent, sometimes containing information that contradicts known reality. Include the Foundation's attempts to determine if this is an actual temporal anomaly or psychological manipulation by a contained entity, and the researcher's struggle to trust their own perception. First person (researcher's perspective with interspersed notes), past tense. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
**SCP Foundation Secure Document** **Item #:** SCP-XXXX **Object Class:** Pending (Temporal/Info-Hazard Investigation) **Researcher:** Dr. Elias Voss, Temporal Anomalies Division **Assigned Site:** Site-17 **Special Containment Procedures:** Dr. Voss is to be monitored at all times via audio-visual surveillance. All personal notes, digital correspondence, and workstation materials are subject to daily review by Site-17 Security. Any anomalous writings matching the description of SCP-XXXX are to be confiscated immediately and analyzed for temporal or memetic contamination. Dr. Voss is restricted from accessing high-clearance containment zones or temporal experimentation labs pending psychological evaluation. --- ### **Incident Report XXXX-1 (Researcher Narrative, Abridged)** **Day 1:** The first note appeared on my desk at 08:47. No cameras captured its arrival—footage from that timestamp shows a 0.3-second gap, just static. The handwriting was mine. Not an imitation, not a close match. *Mine.* > *"Elias—don’t let them recalibrate the Alpha-9 chrono-stabilizer on the 18th. It fails. It all fails."* I checked the logs. The Alpha-9 recalibration *was* scheduled for the 18th. A routine procedure. I reported the note to Security, but by the time they arrived, the paper had dissolved into a fine, odorless ash. No residue. No evidence. **Day 4:** Three more notes. Each appeared during camera malfunctions. The handwriting grew erratic, ink smeared like the writer’s hands were shaking. > *"They don’t tell you about the bodies. The containment breach isn’t just a breach—it’s a cascade. SCP-682 gets out. SCP-106 follows. They’re working together. HOW ARE THEY WORKING TOGETHER?"* I checked the records. SCP-682 and SCP-106 had never shown coordinated behavior. Ever. **Day 7:** The notes started contradicting themselves. > *"Don’t trust Dr. Shirazi. She’s compromised."* Then, two hours later: > *"Shirazi is the only one who knows. Find her before they do."* I knew Shirazi. She was Level 4, Bio-Containment. I’d never spoken to her. **Day 10:** The first bloodstains appeared on the paper. The writing was barely legible. > *"They’re in the walls. They’ve always been in the walls. The cameras don’t see them. The cameras NEVER see them."* I requested a full sweep of my office. Nothing. **Day 14:** Security found me screaming at my reflection in the break room. I don’t remember doing it. They pulled me for psych eval. Dr. Hargrove’s assessment: *"No signs of external memetic influence. Paranoia and temporal disorientation consistent with prolonged exposure to unverified precognitive stimuli."* They didn’t believe me. **Day 18:** The Alpha-9 recalibration proceeded as scheduled. Nothing happened. No breach. No failure. I should have felt relieved. Instead, I found another note. > *"You changed it. But it’s worse now. You don’t remember the other timeline. You never will."* **Day 22:** The notes stopped making sense. > *"The sky is wrong. The sun is black. They’re singing. Make them stop singing."* I requested a transfer. Denied. **Day 25:** The last note wasn’t on paper. It was carved into my forearm. I don’t remember doing it. The cameras glitched for 12 seconds. > *"YOU SHOULDN’T HAVE SAVED US."* --- ### **Addendum XXXX-2 (Security & Research Notes)** - **Temporal Analysis:** No verified temporal anomalies detected in Site-17 during the incident period. However, all note appearances coincide with unexplained surveillance gaps (max 0.5 sec). - **Memetic Screening:** No known infohazard patterns detected in recovered note fragments. Handwriting analysis confirms 98% match to Dr. Voss’s writing. - **Containment Hypothesis:** Possible psychological manipulation by an unknown entity (see SCP-████’s "retroactive memory alteration" effects). Alternatively, Dr. Voss may be experiencing a localized, self-contained temporal recursion event. **Final Note:** Dr. Voss was placed on administrative leave following a violent episode in which he attempted to dismantle his workstation, claiming "the notes are still coming, you just can’t see them yet." As of this report, no further notes have been found. **Pending further investigation.** --- *"Time doesn’t bleed. But we do."* —Recovered fragment, source unknown.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This SCP report demonstrates a strong understanding of the Foundation's clinical documentation style while effectively building psychological horror through escalating paranoia. The piece successfully balances the sterile, bureaucratic tone of SCP reports with the increasingly desperate voice of Dr. Voss, creating an unsettling contrast that serves the narrative well. The structure is well-executed, using the format of containment procedures, incident reports, and addenda to create authenticity. The progression from rational concern to complete psychological breakdown is paced effectively, with each note becoming more desperate and contradictory. The temporal elements are handled cleverly - the notes contradict each other and known reality, leaving genuine ambiguity about whether this is a temporal anomaly or psychological manipulation. The writing maintains consistent voice throughout, with Dr. Voss's clinical observations gradually giving way to fragmented desperation. The imagery is appropriately unsettling without being overwrought - details like the paper dissolving into ash, camera glitches, and the final carved message create effective horror beats. However, the piece has some weaknesses. The character development is somewhat limited by the clinical format, though this is partially intentional. Some of the horror elements, while effective, rely on familiar SCP tropes (reality-bending entities, containment breaches, surveillance gaps). The ending, while appropriately dark, doesn't fully resolve the central mystery in a way that feels completely satisfying. The prose is generally clean and purposeful, avoiding purple prose while maintaining atmospheric tension. The technical aspects of SCP writing are handled competently, with appropriate redactions, classification levels, and bureaucratic language. The piece successfully creates the sense of an unreliable narrator without making the text itself incoherent. + Scp: Unmarked Doors Archive — Score: 74.3
Prompt:
Write an SCP entry about a series of identical unmarked doors appearing in abandoned buildings worldwide that lead to a massive, architecturally impossible archive. Documents within reference a previous global civilization destroyed by an unspecified containment failure. Foundation researchers discover references to their own organization under a different name, including personnel files for current staff dated centuries ago. Include exploration logs revealing sections of the archive actively being removed by entities resembling hazmat teams who flee when approached, and evidence that O5 Council members have visited the archive without authorization. Third person (exploration team perspective) with recovered document excerpts. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
**SCP-XXXX - The Archive of the Lost Protocol** **Item #:** SCP-XXXX **Object Class:** Keter **Special Containment Procedures:** Due to the unpredictable and widespread manifestation of SCP-XXXX access points, full containment is currently unfeasible. Mobile Task Force Mu-13 ("Archivists") is to monitor abandoned structures globally for unmarked doors matching SCP-XXXX's description. Any discovered instances are to be secured under the guise of structural hazard warnings. Civilians attempting entry are to be detained and administered Class-B amnestics. Unauthorized Foundation personnel attempting to access SCP-XXXX are to be reprimanded and subjected to psychological evaluation. Any evidence of O5 Council involvement is to be reported directly to Ethics Committee oversight. **Description:** SCP-XXXX designates a series of identical, unmarked metal doors appearing in abandoned buildings worldwide. Doors lack handles or visible mechanisms but open when pressure is applied. Each leads to the same extradimensional structure: a vast, non-Euclidean archive of unknown origin. The archive consists of endless shelving units containing documents, artifacts, and digital records referencing a pre-existing global civilization (designated *"The First Protocol"*) that achieved technological parity with the Foundation before suffering a catastrophic containment breach. Records describe an entity or event referred to only as *"The Collapse Vector,"* which resulted in near-total annihilation. Of note are personnel files matching current Foundation staff—including birth dates predating their official records by centuries—and references to an organization called *"The Vanguard Commission,"* bearing the Foundation's insignia with minor alterations. **Addendum XXXX-1: Exploration Logs** **Exploration Team:** MTF Mu-13 ("Archivists") **Team Lead:** Captain Elias Voss **Notable Equipment:** GPS beacons, reinforced tethers, Class-IV reality anchors **** **Voss:** Moving in. Door’s open. No resistance. *Team enters a cavernous hall lined with towering shelves. Ceiling is not visible. Lighting is provided by an unknown sourceless glow. Walls shift subtly when not observed directly.* **Researcher Cho:** GPS is useless. Compasses spinning. Recommend tethers. **Voss:** Confirmed. Secure lines. Fan out—document anything with Foundation markings. *Team proceeds. Shelves contain files labeled in an unrecognized script that shifts into legible text upon observation.* **Researcher Cho:** (reading) *"Vanguard Commission Directive 001: The Collapse Vector is not to be named, measured, or observed directly. All personnel must—"* (pauses) This is dated 1843. **Voss:** That’s impossible. Foundation wasn’t— **Researcher Hale:** Captain. You need to see this. *Hale holds a personnel file. Image matches Captain Voss. Birth date listed as "1789."* **Voss:** (agitated) That’s not me. Can’t be. **Cho:** There’s more. O5 profiles. Some of these… they’re current Council members. *Distant metallic clattering. Team turns to observe three humanoid figures in black hazmat gear removing files from a nearby shelf. No insignia visible.* **Voss:** Hey! Identify yourselves! *Figures freeze, then sprint into the stacks. Team pursues but loses them in the shifting architecture.* **Hale:** They took something. This shelf’s been cleared. **Cho:** (examining floor) Drag marks. Like they were moving something heavy. **Voss:** Fall back. We need to report this. *Team returns to entry point. Door is missing. Walls reconfigure, revealing a new corridor.* **Hale:** We’re not where we started. **Voss:** Stay calm. Follow the tethers. *After 27 minutes of navigation, team locates a door matching the original. Exit is successful.* **** **Addendum XXXX-2: Recovered Documents** **Document XXXX-7:** *"Final missive from Director-1 of the Vanguard Commission: The Collapse Vector has breached all barriers. We have failed. To whoever inherits this archive—learn from our mistakes. Do not repeat Protocol 001-Lambda. Do not trust the O5."* **Document XXXX-12:** *Surveillance still recovered from Archive Sector-7. Image depicts O5-3 and O5-7 examining files labeled "Project Phoenix." Time stamp precedes O5-3’s recorded birth by 112 years.* **Addendum XXXX-3: Incident XXXX-9** On ██/██/20██, SCP-XXXX’s primary access door manifested in Site-19’s abandoned Wing D. Security feeds show O5-3 entering alone. No interaction was logged. Door vanished upon exit. O5-3 has declined debriefing. **Research Note:** The Archive is not just a record—it’s a warning. And someone is erasing it piece by piece. —Dr. ██████, Senior Researcher, Department of Temporal Anomalies
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This SCP entry demonstrates a solid understanding of the Foundation's clinical documentation style and successfully incorporates all the major elements requested in the prompt. The piece maintains the characteristic dry, bureaucratic tone throughout while building an intriguing mystery around temporal anomalies and organizational conspiracy. The structure follows proper SCP format with containment procedures, description, and addenda. The exploration log effectively uses dialogue to reveal information naturally, though some exchanges feel slightly mechanical. The recovered documents add authenticity and deepen the mystery surrounding the "Vanguard Commission" and its connection to the current Foundation. The concept of an archive documenting a previous civilization's containment failure is compelling, and the detail about personnel files matching current staff creates genuine unease. The hazmat-suited entities removing documents adds urgency and suggests active suppression of information. The O5 Council's unauthorized involvement provides a satisfying conspiracy element. However, the piece suffers from some predictable beats - the mysterious figures fleeing when approached, the door disappearing to trap the team, and the ominous final research note all feel somewhat formulaic for SCP entries. The dialogue, while functional, lacks distinct character voices and occasionally serves purely expository purposes. The writing is competent but not particularly elegant, prioritizing information delivery over literary flourish - which is appropriate for the format but limits emotional engagement. The imagery is adequate but could be more vivid, particularly in describing the non-Euclidean architecture. The piece maintains coherence throughout and builds tension effectively, though it doesn't reach particularly surprising or innovative territory within the SCP framework. The ending appropriately maintains the Foundation's clinical uncertainty while hinting at larger conspiracies, avoiding inappropriate positivity for the horror genre. + Classic sci-fi: Offworlder (Le Guin) — Score: 83.8
Prompt:
Classic sci-fi: Offworlder (Author style: Le Guin) Write a chapter following a young diplomatic envoy sent to address tensions on a distant human colony where humanity has diverged into distinct subspecies through both natural adaptation and separation of lineages. Against protocol, the envoy slips away from official functions to walk the streets alone, encountering markets, ordinary citizens, and social structures that contradict the official briefings. Upon returning to their quarters, the envoy is reprimanded by Command, and is tasked with approaching the stationed Minister of Science (a political posting rather than scientific). A challenging conversation ensues, in which the envoy's wits and will are tested, by a seasoned political operator looking to test the mettle of the offworlder. Length: 1000 words.
Model Output:
**Chapter Four: The Minister’s Examination** The envoy had been warned not to wander. *Stay with the delegation. Observe protocol. Do not engage without clearance.* But the streets of New Thebes had called to them—narrow, winding, alive with voices that did not speak in the measured tones of diplomacy. The envoy had slipped away after the third ceremonial toast, when the local dignitaries were too deep in their cups to notice. Now, walking back through the embassy gates, they carried the scent of the market with them—spices, molten metal, the faint musk of the riverfolk’s scaled cloaks. Their fingers still tingled from the brush of a merchant’s hand, pressing a scrap of fabric into their palm: deep violet, threaded with gold, a color no Earth-born eye had ever seen before. “You were instructed to remain with the delegation.” The voice came from the shadows of the courtyard. Commandant Vey, arms folded, face unreadable in the dim light of the colony’s twin moons. The envoy straightened. “I observed.” “You *disappeared*.” “I learned.” A pause. The Commandant exhaled through their nose. “The Minister of Science has requested you.” “Why?” “Because you’re an unknown variable. And unknowns make politicians nervous.” --- The Minister’s office was all sharp angles and cold light, a deliberate contrast to the organic sprawl of the city outside. The Minister themself was a lean figure, skin pale from years under artificial lighting, fingers steepled over a desk that looked more like an altar. “Envoy.” The Minister did not smile. “You’ve caused quite the stir.” The envoy inclined their head. “Unintentionally.” “Intentions don’t matter. Only consequences.” The Minister gestured to a chair. “Sit.” They sat. “You walked the river market.” “Yes.” “And what did you see?” The envoy considered. “A woman selling beetles that glow when you whisper to them. A child with six fingers weaving a net. A dispute settled by throwing bones into a fire.” The Minister’s expression did not change. “And what does that tell you?” “That your reports are incomplete.” A flicker—something like amusement, or irritation. “Our reports are precise. You saw outliers. Deviations.” “I saw people.” The Minister leaned forward. “You are here to assess whether this colony remains aligned with Earth’s interests. Not to collect folk tales.” The envoy met their gaze. “Folk tales tell you what people value.” “And what do you think they value here, Envoy?” The envoy reached into their pocket and laid the scrap of violet fabric on the desk. “Something they can’t get from us.” The Minister stared at it. For the first time, something like uncertainty passed over their face. “You took this?” “It was given.” A beat. Then the Minister exhaled, slow and deliberate. “You are either very clever or very reckless.” “Does it matter?” The Minister smiled, thin and sharp. “It will.” They leaned back. “You’ll attend the harvest negotiations tomorrow. Observe. And this time—” Their fingers tapped the fabric. “—remember who you represent.” The envoy stood. “I will.” As they turned to leave, the Minister spoke again, softer: “Tell me, Envoy. Do you think we’re still the same species?” The envoy did not look back. “I think that’s the wrong question.” The door closed behind them.
Judge Evaluation:
[Analysis] This piece demonstrates a strong grasp of Le Guin's distinctive style, particularly her spare, contemplative prose and focus on anthropological observation. The author successfully captures the essence of diplomatic science fiction, where cultural understanding takes precedence over action or spectacle. The adherence to instructions is excellent - all major plot points are hit: the unauthorized wandering, the reprimand, and the challenging conversation with the Minister of Science. The worldbuilding efficiently establishes the colonial setting and hints at human divergence without over-explaining. The characterization is nuanced, particularly the Minister of Science, who emerges as a complex political operator testing the envoy's capabilities. The dialogue crackles with subtext and political maneuvering, avoiding exposition dumps while revealing character motivations. The envoy's responses show growing confidence and diplomatic skill. The prose style authentically echoes Le Guin's approach - clean, precise sentences that carry weight beyond their surface meaning. The imagery is selective but evocative: "beetles that glow when you whisper to them" and the violet fabric serve as concrete symbols of the colony's divergence from Earth norms. The pacing is well-controlled, moving efficiently from the street wandering through the confrontation to the final philosophical exchange. The ending question about species identity perfectly captures the kind of profound uncertainty that drives Le Guin's best work. However, some elements feel slightly underdeveloped. The envoy's transformation from protocol-follower to confident diplomat happens quickly, though this may be appropriate for the chapter format. The worldbuilding, while atmospheric, could benefit from slightly more specificity about the nature of human divergence. The dialogue maintains authenticity throughout, with each character having a distinct voice. The Minister's testing of the envoy feels genuine to political maneuvering, and the envoy's responses demonstrate growing sophistication without feeling unearned.
